Title: High Electric Bills Are the Tip of the Iceberg
URL: https://www.americanthinker.com/articles/2025/02/high_electric_bills_are_the_tip_of_the_iceberg.html
Time Published: 2025-02-14T05:00:00Z
Full Content:
U.S. electric rates are going up. In Missouri, Ameren increased residential power bills by 11% less than two years ago, and now it is seeking another 15% increase, per the Public Service Commission (PSC). According to the U.S. Energy Information Administration (EIA), rate increases were experienced in 43 American states between 2023 and 2024. The EIA also reported record rate increases between 2021 and 2024 projections. In California, the Pacific Gas & Electric Company (PG&E) was granted six rate increases in 2024. Local ABC 30 Action News reported that The Utility Reform Network estimated that residents had experienced a $50 average increase to their bill before the last of these increases took effect. In New York City, Consolidated Edison Inc. (Con Edison) recently proposed an 11.4% rate increase for its electricity service, according to Energy and Environment News by Politico. An 8.79% electric rate increase was recently approved for We Energy (WE) in Wisconsin, a subsidiary of WEC Energy Group, which also serves Illinois, Michigan, and Minnesota, per Wisconsin Public Radio. All of these companies are publicly owned, and they are just a tiny fraction of the American electric companies working to appease their top shareholders: BlackRock and Vanguard. During the Jan. 15 public hearing to discuss Ameren Missouri‚Äôs proposed rate increase, Ameren Missouri vice president of regulatory and legislative affairs Warren Wood noted that the $446-million overall increase was proposed to offer a ‚Äúfair return to shareholders.‚Äù According to Ameren‚Äôs Nasdaq listing, the company‚Äôs top shareholder is Vanguard Group Inc., a global hedge fund investment company focused on assessing ‚Äúclimate risk‚Äù and ‚Äúnet zero emissions.‚Äù BlackRock Inc. is Ameren‚Äôs third top shareholder, another global investment hedge fund focused on climate change. BlackRock Inc. and Vanguard Group Inc. are also the top shareholders of Con Edison, PG&E, and the WEC Energy Group. American Electric Power is the parent company of various local electric companies that serve Americans living in Arkansas, Indiana, Kentucky, Louisiana, Michigan, Ohio, Oklahoma, Tennessee, Texas, Virginia, and West Virginia. According to the Nasdaq, this parent company‚Äôs top shareholders are Vanguard Group Inc. and BlackRock Inc. as well. When cross-referencing every electric company that is a member of the Edison Electric Institute, one pattern is easily recognized: BlackRock and Vanguard are the top shareholders of the majority of American electric companies. And like their shareholders, these energy companies support the business of ‚Äúclean energy.‚Äù Ameren, Con Edison, PG&E, WEC Energy, and American Electric Power have all committed to ‚Äúclean energy‚Äù solutions, without offering a long-term plan on how these sources will be maintained for the future. ‚ÄúClean Energy‚Äù waste has yet to be addressed by companies investing in ‚Äúrenewables.‚Äù It is a new concept even for the United States Environmental Protection Agency. On their website they note that ‚Äúsome end-of-life solar panels contain enough metals, like lead, to meet the definition of hazardous waste under the Resource Conservation and Recovery Act.‚Äù The EPA website also notes the need to update standards for lithium-ion solar battery waste, because ‚Äúthough lithium batteries are generally safe when used, stored, and charged appropriately, these batteries can cause fires when improperly discarded or otherwise mismanaged at the end of their lives.‚Äù The Chemical Abstracts Service (CAS), a division of the American Chemical Society, estimated in 2022 that just 5% of lithium-ion batteries were recycled, adding yet another waste problem for ‚Äúclean energy.‚Äù Add in ecosystem disruption and wildlife loss, and ‚Äúclean energy‚Äù waste is growing into a big problem. Unfortunately, solar power especially has another dirty record: according to the Heritage Foundation, ‚ÄúRoughly 80% of solar components are manufactured in China using slave labor.‚Äù Even the U.S. Department of Labor Bureau of International Labor Affairs states on its website, ‚ÄúNearly half of the world‚Äôs polysilicon, a key material used to produce solar panels, comes from the Xinjiang Uyghur Autonomous Region (XUAR or Xinjiang), a region of China where members of ethnic and religious minority groups are forced by the government to work against their will.‚Äù What‚Äôs more, Congress held a hearing exploring China‚Äôs role in enslaving children and other people in the Democratic Republic of Congo to mine cobalt, a key element in creating lithium-ion batteries. The Congressional-Executive Commission on China (CECC) highlighted key points of the hearing: Around 70% of the world‚Äôs cobalt supply comes from the DRC, and 41% of all batteries containing cobalt are imported from the People‚Äôs Republic of China. CECC chairman Rep. Chris Smith (R-N.J.) stated, ‚ÄúFrom dirt to battery, from cobalt to cars, the entire system is fueled by violence, cruelty, and corruption. ... By ignoring these rights and by treating people including children as expendable, China is committing gross violations of human rights and is seeking to rewrite the international order.‚Äù Journalist Stavros Nicolas Niarchos testified, ‚ÄúI have seen how landscapes have been destroyed, water polluted and air filled with dust and carbon as mining companies rush to extract minerals like copper, cobalt, lithium, and phosphates. Oftentimes, human rights abuses go hand in glove with these environmental catastrophes. ... We must also not forget the very real human rights abuses that attend the extraction of battery metals in the DRC. Children are brutalized, women are violated, and men are subject to wage slavery.‚Äù ‚ÄúClean energy‚Äù investments and human rights violations surrounding Chinese industry are undeniable, and top American energy investors BlackRock and Vanguard are no strangers to China. In 2023, BlackRock and another global investment company, MSCI, were investigated by the House Select Committee on the CCP and found to have profited from ‚Äúfueling China‚Äôs military.‚Äù The committee noted, ‚ÄúBlackRock and MSCI invest or enable the investment of Americans' savings into dozens of blacklisted Chinese companies that threaten US national security or support the Chinese Communist Party's human rights abuses.‚Äù Last year, the House Select Committee on the CCP reported that BlackRock had invested at least $1.9 billion in red-flagged and blacklisted companies that fund the military capabilities of the People‚Äôs Republic of China and aid its human rights violations. The Coalition for a Prosperous America released a Case Study in 2023, which reported that Vanguard and another investment company, FTSE Russell, invested billions in the CCP. The report found that Vanguard specifically funded dozens of Chinese military subsidiaries and eight Chinese companies that had been blacklisted due to their violations of the Uyghur Forced Labor Prevention Act (UFLPA). The top shareholders of publicly traded American energy companies have been linked to funding the nation‚Äôs largest adversary and its human rights violations. Meanwhile, Americans have been unknowingly footing the bill. But there is another way. Electric Co-Ops are being formed all over the nation. These give residents the power. Instead of publicly trading American energy to any globalist CCP-supporting hedge fund, co-ops are owned by the residents who pay into them. No globalist interference, no slave labor products. Right now, most of us have only a single electricity option, and these publicly traded monopolies are working against us. But it doesn‚Äôt have to be this way. We can form more energy co-ops and escape the technocratic globalists preying on publicly traded electric companies, and we can power our homes our way without compromising American values. Image: Axel Rouvin via Flickr, CC BY 2.0. U.S. electric rates are going up. In Missouri, Ameren increased residential power bills by 11% less than two years ago, and now it is seeking another 15% increase, per the Public Service Commission (PSC). According to the U.S. Energy Information Administration (EIA), rate increases were experienced in 43 American states between 2023 and 2024. The EIA also reported record rate increases between 2021 and 2024 projections. In California, the Pacific Gas & Electric Company (PG&E) was granted six rate increases in 2024. Local ABC 30 Action News reported that The Utility Reform Network estimated that residents had experienced a $50 average increase to their bill before the last of these increases took effect. In New York City, Consolidated Edison Inc. (Con Edison) recently proposed an 11.4% rate increase for its electricity service, according to Energy and Environment News by Politico. An 8.79% electric rate increase was recently approved for We Energy (WE) in Wisconsin, a subsidiary of WEC Energy Group, which also serves Illinois, Michigan, and Minnesota, per Wisconsin Public Radio. Title: Franklin Templeton‚Äôs money market fund launches on Solana ‚Äì Is BlackRock losing ground?
URL: https://ambcrypto.com/franklin-templetons-money-market-fund-launches-on-solana-is-blackrock-losing-ground/
Time Published: 2025-02-14T03:00:40Z
Full Content:
With $1.6 trillion under management, why is Franklin Templeton doubling down on blockchain? Franklin Templeton has expanded its tokenized money market fund, Franklin OnChain US Government Money Fund (FOBXX), to the Solana [SOL] blockchain, further strengthening its presence in the digital asset space. With $1.6 trillion in assets under management, the firm announced this move on the 12th of February, building on FOBXX‚Äôs multi-chain strategy. Originally launched in 2021, the fund has already integrated with Ethereum [ETH], Coinbase‚Äôs Base, Aptos [APT], and Avalanche [AVAX], while Stellar [XLM] remains its primary blockchain. Thus, as the third-largest tokenized money market fund, FOBXX is nearing a total asset value of $600 million, highlighting its growing adoption. Additionally, it also holds the distinction of being the world‚Äôs first mutual fund to leverage blockchain technology for transaction processing and share ownership recording, with each share represented by a BENJI token. Remarking on the same, Franklin Templeton took to X (formerly Twitter) and said, ‚ÄúNew chain unlocked. BENJI is now live on solana! Solana is a fast, secure and censorship resistant Layer 1 blockchain encouraging global adoption via its open infrastructure.‚Äù Needless to say, institutional interest in the Solana network has been on the rise, signaling a shift beyond its reputation as a hub for memecoins. In Q3 2024, investments in decentralized applications built on SOL surged by 54%, reaching $173 million, reflecting growing confidence among wealth managers and hedge funds. The token itself has staged a remarkable recovery from the bear market lows of under $10 following FTX‚Äôs collapse. It recently hit a 52-week high of $265.10, partly fueled by excitement surrounding former U.S. President Donald Trump‚Äôs memecoin launch on the network. Additionally, Solana has emerged as the dominant platform for launching new tokens, particularly within decentralized trading. A report from Pantera Capital revealed that SOL now accounts for over 90% of new tokens listed on decentralized exchanges‚Äîan extraordinary jump from just 1% at the end of 2023. Echoing similar sentiments, Cosmo Jiang and Eric Wallach in the same report noted, ‚ÄúEven when innovation doesn‚Äôt start on Solana, it eventually finds its way there.‚Äù However, as the firm strengthens its foothold, it faces growing competition from BlackRock‚Äôs BUIDL fund, which has surged past Franklin‚Äôs BENJI token in market capitalization, reaching $637 million. With tokenized treasury products now totaling $3.6 billion, the race for dominance in this emerging sector is intensifying. Beyond its money market fund, Franklin Templeton has been actively expanding its crypto offerings, launching Bitcoin [BTC] and Ethereum [ETH] ETFs while seeking SEC approval for a Crypto Index ETF. Its latest move‚Äîa Delaware-based trust linked to a Solana ETF‚Äîfurther highlights its strategic push into blockchain-based investment products. Therefore, as institutions embrace tokenized assets, Franklin Templeton‚Äôs innovation could help shape the future of digital finance. Players can now go into Blackwing Lair and change any Tier 2 items with Tier 1 set bonuses back into the Tier 2 item with Tier 2 set bonuses. Draught of the Sands for Hunters and Rogues will no longer erroneously stack under certain conditions. Unbalancing Strike from the Twin Emperors encounter in the Temple of Ahn‚ÄôQiraj will no longer affect the bonus attack power or spell damage gained from Defender‚Äôs Resolve. You will always gain these stats based on your pre-Unbalancing Strike defense skill. Druid Hunter Mage Priest Rogue Shaman Warlock December 9, 2024 Season of Discovery December 10, 2024 Season of Discovery December 11, 2024 Season of Discovery December 9, 2024 Season of Discovery The hotfix above was implemented to make it so that the Mixology benefit (where an Alchemist could create 2-5 flasks if they had completed the required quest) now works correctly. It was not working before, due to the stack limitation. Your local Alchemist was not holding out on you, they just weren‚Äôt getting procs until the fix above was implemented. Reminder, this is a Premium article and requires a subscription to read. Vulcan Steel sees green shoots emerging. Photo / NZME The reporting season gets under way in earnest next week, but results so far have given a glimpse as to what might lie ahead. Steel distributor Vulcan Steel is seen as a bellwether for the economy, and despite a first-half profit slump, the company‚Äôs share price has been on the up, post-result. Vulcan said Australia and New Zealand were at a turning point. It added trading volumes in New Zealand were anticipated to recover from the second or third quarter of this calendar year. Salt Funds managing director Matt Goodson said it‚Äôs not the first time Vulcan has cried ‚Äúgreen shoots‚Äù. But going on the stronger share price, post result, it looked like the market believed it, he said. Goodson said the company‚Äôs exposure to the rural economy, particularly the strong dairy sector, made the ‚Äúgreen shoots‚Äù story more credible. More light will be shed on the state of the economy next week when some of the market‚Äôs bigger companies report. ‚ÄúEverything we‚Äôve seen sort of suggests the September quarter was the bottom. December was still a bit bumpy though,‚Äù Goodson said. ‚ÄúThere are some signs of life, some not so good. Retail still looked a bit ugly in the December quarter. ‚ÄúIt‚Äôs not so much the results themselves, but the strength and conviction around the forward statements.‚Äù Goodson said it would take until the second half of this year for the full impact of the Reserve Bank‚Äôs sharp rate cuts to take effect. ‚ÄúSo that‚Äôs probably the single key thematic at the moment.‚Äù A2 Milk, which listed on the NZX back in 2004, is set to announce its first dividend at Monday‚Äôs first-half result. And with $968.9 million sitting in the bank (at last count) - why not? Last November, a2 Milk said its 2025 full-year revenue guidance was trading ahead of plan. Its previous guidance, issued in August, was for mid single-digit revenue growth in 2025 versus 2024. A2 Milk‚Äôs new dividend policy targets a payout ratio range of between 60% and 80% of normalised net profit. Aside from its dividend plans, a2 Milk has also raised the possibility of supply chain acquisitions or joint ventures to augment its Mataura Valley Milk facility in Southland. Forsyth Barr senior analyst Matt Montgomerie said he‚Äôs not expecting any surprises on Monday, relative to consensus expectations or the company‚Äôs own guidance. ‚ÄúThis is a brave assertion to make given a2 Milk‚Äôs track record on result days, but the (still) pending supply chain acquisition/JV is the main area of possible surprise,‚Äù he said in a preview. He said the key focus areas were a2 Milk‚Äôs supply chain updates, China label infant formula revenue, and the English Label (EL) outlook in light of the new Genesis HMO product, a milk drink aimed at toddlers aged 1 year and over. The market consensus for Monday‚Äôs result is for half-year of revenue of $870.2m, up from $812.1m a year earlier, steady underlying Ebitda (earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation, and amortisation) at about $113.8m, up 2%, and a net profit of $77.7m, up 1%. The company‚Äôs first dividend is expected to be about 7c a share. For the big power generators, the second half of last year was fraught with challenges - a gas shortage, coupled with very low lake levels and light wind conditions - which saw wholesale prices go through the roof. This week, the big four power companies said they had teamed up to look at ways of extending the life of Genesis Energy‚Äôs coal and gas-fired Rankines at Huntly to improve security of supply. ‚ÄúI think it sort of really illustrates in New Zealand where it‚Äôs absolutely in the country‚Äôs interests that those turbines be refurbished and still be around come 2040,‚Äù Salt Funds' Goodson said. ‚ÄúClearly, it‚Äôs going to need Commerce Commission authorisation to do so, so there is this really interesting tension between market efficiency and the best outcomes versus competition.‚Äù In terms of first-half results, Contact gets the ball rolling on Monday. Big volumes of stock look likely to trade, courtesy of the influential passive funds, in the lead-up to the change. On the international scene, the big issue facing investors is what the US Federal Reserve does next after a surprisingly strong inflation outturn - 3% for the year to January - which drove US 10-year bond yields up by 10 basis points. The market had been pricing two more rate cuts this year from the Fed, but the data, which is yet to reflect the likely inflationary effect of new US tariffs, means people are beginning to question the likely track. The Reserve Bank of Australia is expected to cut its official rate, which has been at 4.35% since November 2023, on Tuesday with the Reserve Bank of NZ expected to cut its Official Cash Rate by half a percent the following day. If the differential between New Zealand and US rates widens, still more downward pressure is expected to mount on the already weak Kiwi dollar, which should provide still more impetus for local exporters. AIA is due to report its interim result on February 20. Meanwhile, the giant international fund BlackRock has raised its stake in AIA to 9.19% from 8.17%. The company had previously updated its earnings guidance on underlying net profit after tax (underlying Npat) for the year ending September 30, 2025. Tower‚Äôs full-year underlying net profit forecast was revised upwards to a range of between $60m and $70m, from the previously advised range of $50m to $60m. Title: The Energy Transition Is Unstoppable‚ÄîBut Are We Moving Fast Enough?
URL: https://energycentral.com/c/ec/energy-transition-unstoppable%E2%80%94-are-we-moving-fast-enough
Time Published: 2025-02-13T15:57:00Z
Full Content:
This group brings together the best thinkers on energy and climate. Join us for smart, insightful posts and conversations about where the energy industry is and where it is going. Post Tom Raftery works at the intersection of technology and sustainability. Tom researches and advises companies on the clean energy transition. Tom also keynotes international events, chairs panels... Energy. The lifeblood of civilisation. The force that propels economies, lights up megacities, keeps your phone buzzing at 2 AM. And yet, the entire system‚Äîthe backbone of modern life‚Äîis cracking, shifting, warping into something entirely new. Fossil fuels, the undisputed rulers of the past century, are on their way out. But are they leaving fast enough? That‚Äôs the billion, no, trillion-dollar question. I just sat down with Jarand Rystad, Founder and CEO of Rystad Energy, a guy who doesn‚Äôt just observe the global energy chessboard‚Äîhe helps define the moves. We ripped into the hard questions: Is the energy transition accelerating at a breakneck pace, or are we still stuck in second gear? Are policy missteps slowing progress? And crucially, do we have a chance in hell of outrunning climate catastrophe? Spoiler alert: The energy revolution is in full swing. But momentum alone won‚Äôt save us. The stakes? Higher than ever. Wildfires torching landscapes. Supercharged storms rewriting coastlines. Energy markets seesawing in chaos. The transition isn‚Äôt some academic exercise‚Äîit‚Äôs the fulcrum upon which our collective future teeters. Why This Shift Is Unstoppable Conventional wisdom says the energy transition is a political affair‚Äîgovernments pushing green policies, activists waving placards. Nice story, but wrong. Economics is the real kingmaker. And the numbers? Staggering. ‚úîÔ∏è Solar & Wind: The Price Tag Tells the Story ‚Äì Forget subsidies. Forget government mandates. In 2024, renewables are just‚Ä¶cheaper. Solar costs have imploded, free-falling by 81% between 2009-2019 and it has continued to fall precipitously year on year since (thanks, BloombergNEF). Wind isn‚Äôt far behind. This isn‚Äôt a ‚Äúgreen‚Äù decision anymore. It‚Äôs a financial one. ‚úîÔ∏è Batteries: The Gamechanger That‚Äôs Already Here ‚Äì Ten years ago, the idea of storing renewable power for later use felt like sci-fi. Now? Lithium-ion battery costs have nosedived by over 90% between 2010-2023 (IRENA says hello). Grid-scale storage is no longer theoretical‚Äîit‚Äôs happening. ‚úîÔ∏è Fossil Fuel Investing? A Sinking Ship ‚Äì Once a safe bet, now a financial minefield. Oil and gas markets swing wildly, spooking investors‚Äîsome of whom are doubling down on renewables, while others hesitate amid shifting political tides. BlackRock, Vanguard, and Wall Street‚Äôs biggest players had been making decisive moves into clean energy, but with the new U.S. administration recalibrating policies, some are slowing their green pivot, waiting to see how regulations shake out. Jarand Rystad put it plainly: If climate change weren‚Äôt even a thing, the energy transition would still be happening. It‚Äôs simple‚Äîclean tech is cheaper, faster, smarter. But don‚Äôt pop the champagne yet. The road ahead? Riddled with potholes. Three Colossal Roadblocks (And Why They Matter) 1Ô∏è‚É£ China: Renewable Powerhouse or Coal Addict? China is a paradox wrapped in a contradiction. In 2024 alone, they threw 357 GW of renewables onto the grid‚Äîmore than the entire historical solar & wind capacity of the U.S. (around 310 GW, for context). But‚Äîand here‚Äôs the kicker‚Äîthey‚Äôre still greenlighting new coal plants. Why? Two words: Energy security. No country wants rolling blackouts. The problem isn‚Äôt building renewables; it‚Äôs making them reliable. Storage, grid flexibility, and high-voltage transmission lines are the missing pieces. And until those systems scale up, coal remains the crutch. 2Ô∏è‚É£ Hydrogen & Carbon Capture: Savior or Overhyped Distraction? üîπ Hydrogen sounds sexy, but let‚Äôs be real‚Äîit‚Äôs not powering your house or your EV. It‚Äôs expensive, inefficient, and, outside of industries like steel or aviation, it‚Äôs a square peg in a round hole. Electrification beats hydrogen in most scenarios. Every. Single. Time. üîπ Carbon capture? More theory than practice. Sure, we can trap CO‚ÇÇ from cement plants, but direct air capture is still a financial nightmare. Betting on carbon capture to save fossil fuels? Like trying to bail out a sinking ship with a leaky, cracked, coffee cup. 3Ô∏è‚É£ AI & Data Centres: The Hidden Energy Guzzler AI is rewriting industries, sure. But it‚Äôs also rewriting the global energy demand curve. By 2030, data centres could devour 8% of global electricity. That‚Äôs terrifying. The solution? Smart AI (hello DeepSeek, or similar) that uses very little electricity itself, and optimises power use, grids running on renewables, and better hardware efficiency. Otherwise, AI‚Äôs rapid rise could backfire, slamming the brakes on emissions reductions elsewhere. So What Needs to Happen‚ÄîYesterday? ‚úîÔ∏è Fossil Fuel Subsidies Need to Die ‚Äì Governments are still dumping $7 trillion (yes, with a ‚ÄòT‚Äô) into fossil fuel subsidies (IMF stats). Imagine if even half of that went to renewables, storage, and transmission? Game over for coal and oil. ‚úîÔ∏è Investment Needs to Go Supersonic ‚Äì We hit $1.8 trillion in clean energy investment in 2023. Sounds great? Not even close. The IEA says we need $4 trillion per year by 2030. That means doubling down‚Äîfast. ‚úîÔ∏è Grid Infrastructure Needs a Revolution ‚Äì Renewables don‚Äôt work like fossil fuels. They‚Äôre intermittent, decentralised, and demand a smarter grid. We need better transmission lines (and optimized use of those lines), AI-driven power distribution, and massive battery deployments. This isn‚Äôt an option‚Äîit‚Äôs a requirement. The Verdict? We‚Äôre Winning, But Not Fast Enough Solar and wind are smashing fossil fuels on cost. China‚Äôs renewable buildout is staggering. Investors are funneling capital into clean energy like never before. But time is the one thing we don‚Äôt have. The 1.5¬∞C climate goal? Almost out of reach. Global emissions? Still stubbornly high. And policy chaos? Threatens to slow everything down. The next 10 years are make-or-break. The choices made right now will determine whether we head towards a livable future‚Äîor lock in climate chaos for generations. Want the full deep dive? Listen to my full conversation with Jarand Rystad. What‚Äôs your take? Are we sprinting fast enough‚Äîor still crawling towards the finish line? Drop your thoughts in the comments. This post was first published on TomRaftery.com. Photo credit Wayne S. Grazio on Flickr If we had a time machine and could ensure that this rate of acceleration for clean energy happened 10 years earlier than it did, we might be in prime position. But given a lot of the intertia we felt, I agree that we're still lagging unfortunately behind Absolutely agree‚Äîif we had accelerated at this pace a decade earlier, we'd be in a far stronger position today. Unfortunately, inertia, policy delays, and legacy investments slowed progress. The key now is to avoid repeating those mistakes and scale even faster. That said, momentum is finally on renewables' side‚Äîcosts have plummeted, investment is surging, and even historically slow-moving sectors like heavy industry are making shifts. The challenge? Ensuring that policy, infrastructure, and financing move at the same speed as technology. Do you think the current pace is enough to close the gap, or are we still underestimating the scale of change needed? Title: Will Corporate Purpose Go The Way Of DEI?
URL: https://www.forbes.com/sites/iese/2025/02/13/will-corporate-purpose-go-the-way-of-dei/
Time Published: 2025-02-13T15:55:40Z
Full Content:
A movement which gained momentum in the wake of the 2008 financial crisis, corporate purpose speaks ... [+] to the very reason a company exists. With diversity, equity and inclusion (DEI) initiatives under fire, will corporate purpose be next? U.S. President Donald Trump has ordered DEI initiatives be eliminated from government agencies and programs at a time when companies such as Boeing, Harley-Davidson, Target, Tractor Supply, Meta and Walmart, to name a few, are reassessing their commitments and values. If many companies appeared to embrace DEI ‚Äì often under pressure and without deep conviction ‚Äì following the death of George Floyd in 2020, that is changing now as societal and political winds shift to the right. How will this anti-DEI wave impact corporate purpose? In the face of backlash against DEI, is purpose at risk? Are we witnessing a return to profit maximization as the sole goal of business? Abandoning purpose would be a mistake. A movement which gained momentum in the wake of the 2008 financial crisis, corporate purpose is complex and multifaceted. While many companies signed on to DEI policies and environmental initiatives as ways to "check the box" on purpose, it goes beyond these societal goals that are now so polarizing. Instead, purpose speaks to the very reason a company exists. Broadly, corporate purpose can be understood through two perspectives: an outside-in approach, which emphasizes responding to external societal and systemic challenges, and an inside-out approach, which focuses on how a company's internal values and member motivations shape its daily operations to serve customers. The outside-in approach positions corporate purpose as a tool to help address important global challenges such as climate change and social justice. But it can become coercive and thus politically charged. Since government policy is involved in these systemic challenges, private and political interests may come into play, creating potential for disagreement both within and outside organizations. A lesson from the current backlash is that in democratic societies, when the societal stakes for different purposes are high, it is important not to run too far ahead of the electorate and to engage instead in transparent deliberation with slow-moving dissenters. The inside-out approach views purpose as a powerful driver of passion and energy, aligning employees‚Äô personal values with the organization‚Äôs overarching goals. For example, under Hubert Joly‚Äôs leadership, Best Buy‚Äôs purposeextended beyond selling products to improving customers‚Äô lives through technology. A key advantage of the inside-out approach is its ability to foster unity, both within the organization and with external stakeholders, as it is freely chosen by all, and is less likely to spark disagreement. That unity and inspiration should in turn bring greater engagement and productivity. While an inside-out purpose for corporations has many advantages in driving engagement and internal cohesion, it is not easy to draw all the motivational strength from it so that it can be sustainable in an organization that expects also business results. That requires not only defining a purpose thoughtfully but also internalizing and implementing it effectively. Only in this way there is a chance of creating win-wins for shareholders and other stakeholders. Here‚Äôs how to begin: Corporate purpose may be understood through two approaches: outside-in and inside-out. It may be useful for business leaders to look at models of purpose-driven organizations, companies that are financially successful but that counteract the pressure of profit maximization as the default objective of the firm. In implementing purpose, head, heart and hands must be involved. ISS, a facility support services company, defines its purpose as ‚Äúconnecting people and places to make the world work better.‚Äù By framing their purpose as an enabler of better work and life experiences for people, ISS ensures it is both inspiring and strategically aligned with their business objectives, serving as a guiding principle for decision-making. Definining the purpose is the head part of purpose. ISS also engages the heart by fostering an emotional connection to the purpose; by, for example, creating a culture of appreciation, recognition and community through its "Thank You Way" initiative, in which managers and clients send periodic tokens of gratitude to employees. ISS also trains employees to view their roles as opportunities to create positive experiences for clients and end users, ensuring that their purpose is reflected in every task, from cleaning offices to managing facilities. By making purpose actionable - hands - ISS demonstrates that it isn‚Äôt just an abstract ideal but a practical framework guiding how they work every day. Three years ago BlackRock chairman and chief executive Larry Fink advised CEOs: ‚ÄúIt is more important than ever that your company and its management be guided by its purpose.‚Äù Although Fink himself has weathered bruising criticism of his views on sustainable investing and stakeholder capitalism ‚Äì while delivering record results for the asset manager ‚Äì his words on corporate purpose still ring true. By John Almandoz, professor in the Department of Managing People in Organizations of IESE Business School, and Carlos Rey, professor of Strategic Management at the Universitat Internacional de Catalunya (UIC).
